Ten years ago, the younger son was \( s - 10 \) years old, and the older son was \( (s + 2) - 10 = s - 8 \) years old.

\[ 6s - 54 = f - 10 \]

\[ f = 6s - 44 \]

325 OUTPUT: So I've got this problem here. Two people are walking together, and their steps measure 75 cm and 90 cm respectively. I need to find out the minimum distance they should walk so that both can cover the same distance in complete steps. Hmm, that sounds like I need to find a common multiple of their step lengths.

First, I should recall what a multiple is. A multiple of a number is what you get when you multiply that number by any whole number. So, for example, multiples of 75 would be 75, 150, 225, 300, and so on, depending on what you multiply 75 by.

Similarly, multiples of 90 would be 90, 180, 270, 360, and so forth.

Now, I need to find a distance where both can complete their steps without having to take a partial step. That means the distance should be a multiple of both 75 and 90.

The smallest such distance would be the least common multiple (LCM) of 75 and 90. LCM is the smallest number that is a multiple of both numbers.

To find the LCM of two numbers, I can use the formula that involves their greatest common divisor (GCD). The formula is:

\[ \text{LCM}(a,b) = \frac{a \times b}{\text{GCD}(a,b)} \]

So, I need to find the GCD of 75 and 90 first.

Let's find the GCD of 75 and 90.

I can list the factors of each number and find the highest common factor.

Factors of 75: 1, 3, 5, 15, 25, 75.

Now, GCD(168, 112).

168 divided by 112 is 1, since 112 * 1 = 112, and 168 - 112 = 56. So, 168 mod 112 = 56.
